</td></tr></tbody></table><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div>
<p><b>Yasiin Bey</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/j/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;yes&#39;">j</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/iː/: &#39;ee&#39; in &#39;fleece&#39;">iː</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/eɪ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;face&#39;">eɪ</span></span>/</a></span></span>; born <b>Dante Terrell Smith</b>, December 11, 1973), more commonly known by his former stage name <b>Mos Def</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="&#39;m&#39; in &#39;my&#39;">m</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/ɛ/: &#39;e&#39; in &#39;dress&#39;">ɛ</span><span title="&#39;f&#39; in &#39;find&#39;">f</span></span>/</a></span></span>), is an American rapper, singer, songwriter, and actor. His hip hop career began in 1994, alongside his siblings in the short-lived <a href="/wiki/Rap_group" class="mw-redirect" title="Rap group">rap group</a> Urban Thermo Dynamics (UTD), after which they appeared on albums by <a href="/wiki/Da_Bush_Babees" title="Da Bush Babees">Da Bush Babees</a> and <a href="/wiki/De_La_Soul" title="De La Soul">De La Soul</a>. He formed the duo <a href="/wiki/Black_Star_(rap_duo)" title="Black Star (rap duo)">Black Star</a>, alongside fellow <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>-based rapper <a href="/wiki/Talib_Kweli" title="Talib Kweli">Talib Kweli</a>, and in 1998 they released their debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Mos_Def_%26_Talib_Kweli_Are_Black_Star" title="Mos Def &amp; Talib Kweli Are Black Star">Mos Def &amp; Talib Kweli Are Black Star</a></i>, featuring the singles "<a href="/wiki/Definition_(song)" title="Definition (song)">Definition</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Respiration_(song)" title="Respiration (song)">Respiration</a>". He was featured on the roster of <a href="/wiki/Rawkus_Records" title="Rawkus Records">Rawkus Records</a> and in 1999 released his solo debut, <i><a href="/wiki/Black_on_Both_Sides" title="Black on Both Sides">Black on Both Sides</a></i>. His debut was followed by <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Danger" title="The New Danger">The New Danger</a></i> (2004), <i><a href="/wiki/True_Magic" title="True Magic">True Magic</a></i> (2006), and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ecstatic" title="The Ecstatic">The Ecstatic</a></i> (2009).<sup id="cite_ref-ALLMUSIC_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ALLMUSIC-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/About.com" class="mw-redirect" title="About.com">About.com</a> listed him 14th on its "50 Greatest Rappers of All Time".<sup id="cite_ref-:1_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> His hits include "<a href="/wiki/Oh_No_(Mos_Def_and_Pharoahe_Monch_song)" title="Oh No (Mos Def and Pharoahe Monch song)">Oh No</a>", "<a href="/wiki/Ms._Fat_Booty" title="Ms. Fat Booty">Ms. Fat Booty</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/Mathematics_(Mos_Def_song)" title="Mathematics (Mos Def song)">Mathematics</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He was a child actor in television films, sitcoms, and <a href="/wiki/Theater" class="mw-redirect" title="Theater">theater</a>. Since the early 2000s, he has appeared in the films <i><a href="/wiki/Something_the_Lord_Made" title="Something the Lord Made">Something the Lord Made</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Next_Day_Air" title="Next Day Air">Next Day Air</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hitchhiker%27s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy_(film)" title="The Hitchhiker&#39;s Guide to the Galaxy (film)">The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/16_Blocks" title="16 Blocks">16 Blocks</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Be_Kind_Rewind" title="Be Kind Rewind">Be Kind Rewind</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Italian_Job_(2003_film)" title="The Italian Job (2003 film)">The Italian Job</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Woodsman_(2004_film)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Woodsman (2004 film)">The Woodsman</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Bamboozled" title="Bamboozled">Bamboozled</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Brown_Sugar_(2002_film)" title="Brown Sugar (2002 film)">Brown Sugar</a></i> and in television series such as <i><a href="/wiki/Dexter_(TV_series)" title="Dexter (TV series)">Dexter</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/House_(TV_series)" title="House (TV series)">House</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> He hosted <i><a href="/wiki/Def_Poetry_Jam" title="Def Poetry Jam">Def Poetry Jam</a></i> from 2002 to 2007.
</p><p>Bey has been vocal on several social and political causes, including <a href="/wiki/Police_brutality_in_the_United_States" title="Police brutality in the United States">police brutality</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_exceptionalism" title="American exceptionalism">American exceptionalism</a>, and the status of <a href="/wiki/African_Americans" title="African Americans">African Americans</a>.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mos_Def&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Yasiin Bey was born Dante Terrell Smith on December 11, 1973, in <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>, New York City,<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> the son of Sheron Smith and Abdulrahman Smith.<sup id="cite_ref-beliefnet_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beliefnet-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The eldest of 12 children and step-children, he was raised by his mother in Brooklyn, while his father lived in New Jersey.<sup id="cite_ref-Spin_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spin-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>His father was initially a member of the <a href="/wiki/Nation_of_Islam" title="Nation of Islam">Nation of Islam</a> and later followed Imam <a href="/wiki/Warith_Deen_Mohammed" title="Warith Deen Mohammed">Warith Deen Mohammed</a>, who merged into the mainstream <a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni Islam</a> from the Nation of Islam. Bey was not exposed to Islam until the age of 13. He is close friends with fellow <a href="/wiki/Islam_and_hip_hop_in_the_United_States" title="Islam and hip hop in the United States">Muslim hip-hop artists</a> <a href="/wiki/Ali_Shaheed_Muhammad" title="Ali Shaheed Muhammad">Ali Shaheed Muhammad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Q-Tip_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Q-Tip (rapper)">Q-Tip</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-beliefnet_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beliefnet-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bey attended middle school at <a href="/wiki/Philippa_Schuyler#Legacy" title="Philippa Schuyler">Philippa Schuyler Middle School</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bushwick,_Brooklyn" title="Bushwick, Brooklyn">Bushwick, Brooklyn</a>, where he developed his love for acting.<sup id="cite_ref-Spin_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spin-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RS_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> After returning from filming <i>You Take the Kids</i> in Los Angeles, and getting into a relationship with an older girl, Bey dropped out of high school during sophomore year.<sup id="cite_ref-Spin_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spin-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Growing up in New York City, during the <a href="/wiki/Crack_epidemic" class="mw-redirect" title="Crack epidemic">crack epidemic</a> of the 1980s and early 1990s, he has spoken about witnessing widespread instances of gang violence, theft, and poverty in society, which he largely avoided by working on plays, <a href="/wiki/Off-Off-Broadway" class="mw-redirect" title="Off-Off-Broadway">Off-Off-Broadway</a> and arts programs.<sup id="cite_ref-RS_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In a particularly traumatic childhood experience, Bey witnessed his then five-year-old younger brother, Ilias Bey (born Denard Smith), get hit by a car. Ilias later adopted the alias DCQ and was described by Bey as "my first partner in hip hop".<sup id="cite_ref-RS_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RS-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_career">Music career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mos_Def&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Music career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Black_Star_(rap_duo)" title="Black Star (rap duo)">Black Star (rap duo)</a></div>

<h3><span id="1994.E2.80.931998:_Beginnings_with_Rawkus_and_Black_Star"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1994–1998:_Beginnings_with_Rawkus_and_Black_Star">1994–1998: Beginnings with Rawkus and Black Star</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mos_Def&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1994–1998: Beginnings with Rawkus and Black Star">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bey began his music career in 1994, forming the group UTD (or Urban Thermo Dynamics) along with younger brother DCQ and high-school friend Ces.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, they released the album <i>Manifest Destiny</i>, their first and only release to date. The album features a compilation of previously unreleased and re-released tracks recorded during the original UTD run.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1996, Bey emerged as a solo artist and worked with <a href="/wiki/De_La_Soul" title="De La Soul">De La Soul</a> and <a href="/wiki/Da_Bush_Babees" title="Da Bush Babees">Da Bush Babees</a>, before he released his own first single, "Universal Magnetic" in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mos_def-11-mika.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Mos_def-11-mika.jpg/220px-Mos_def-11-mika.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Mos_def-11-mika.jpg/330px-Mos_def-11-mika.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Mos_def-11-mika.jpg/440px-Mos_def-11-mika.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1073" data-file-height="719" /></a><figcaption>Yasiin Bey in 1999</figcaption></figure>
<p>Bey signed with <a href="/wiki/Rawkus_Records" title="Rawkus Records">Rawkus Records</a> and formed the rap group <a href="/wiki/Black_Star_(rap_duo)" title="Black Star (rap duo)">Black Star</a> with <a href="/wiki/Talib_Kweli" title="Talib Kweli">Talib Kweli</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The duo released an album, <i><a href="/wiki/Mos_Def_%26_Talib_Kweli_Are_Black_Star" title="Mos Def &amp; Talib Kweli Are Black Star">Mos Def &amp; Talib Kweli Are Black Star</a></i>, in 1998.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Mostly <a href="/wiki/Music_production" class="mw-redirect" title="Music production">produced</a> by <a href="/wiki/Hi-Tek" title="Hi-Tek">Hi-Tek</a>, the album featured the singles "<a href="/wiki/Respiration_(song)" title="Respiration (song)">Respiration</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Definition_(song)" title="Definition (song)">Definition</a>", which both reached in the Billboard <a href="/wiki/Hot_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Songs" title="Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs">Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs</a> chart.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="1999.E2.80.932006:_Solo_career_and_various_projects"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1999–2006:_Solo_career_and_various_projects">1999–2006: Solo career and various projects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mos_Def&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1999–2006: Solo career and various projects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Bey released his solo debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Black_on_Both_Sides" title="Black on Both Sides">Black on Both Sides</a></i> in October 1999, also through Rawkus.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic1_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic1-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The single "<a href="/wiki/Ms._Fat_Booty" title="Ms. Fat Booty">Ms. Fat Booty</a>" charted,<sup id="cite_ref-:0_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> while the album reached #25 on the Billboard 200.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_200_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_200-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Around this time, he also contributed to the <a href="/wiki/Scritti_Politti" title="Scritti Politti">Scritti Politti</a> album <i>Anomie &amp; Bonhomie</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mos_Def-Rock_The_Bells.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Mos_Def-Rock_The_Bells.jpg/220px-Mos_Def-Rock_The_Bells.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="391" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Mos_Def-Rock_The_Bells.jpg/330px-Mos_Def-Rock_The_Bells.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Mos_Def-Rock_The_Bells.jpg/440px-Mos_Def-Rock_The_Bells.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="800" /></a><figcaption>Yasiin Bey performing at Rock the Bells in New York</figcaption></figure>
<p>In January 2002, Rawkus Records was taken over by <a href="/wiki/Geffen_Records" title="Geffen Records">Geffen Records</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> which released his second solo album <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Danger" title="The New Danger">The New Danger</a></i> in October 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> It included contributions by <a href="/wiki/Shuggie_Otis" title="Shuggie Otis">Shuggie Otis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bernie_Worrell" title="Bernie Worrell">Bernie Worrell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doug_Wimbish" title="Doug Wimbish">Doug Wimbish</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Will_Calhoun" title="Will Calhoun">Will Calhoun</a> as the Black Jack Johnson Band.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> The album reached #5 on the Billboard 200, making it the most successful for the artist to date.<sup id="cite_ref-Billboard_200_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_200-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The single "Sex, Love &amp; Money" charted,<sup id="cite_ref-:0_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and was nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Mos Def's final solo album for <a href="/wiki/Geffen_Records" title="Geffen Records">Geffen Records</a>, titled <i><a href="/wiki/True_Magic" title="True Magic">True Magic</a></i>, was released in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2007.E2.80.932011:_Good_Music_era_and_name_change"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2007–2011:_Good_Music_era_and_name_change">2007–2011: Good Music era and name change</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mos_Def&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2007–2011: Good Music era and name change">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On November 7, 2007, Bey performed live in San Francisco at The Mezzanine venue. The performance was recorded for an upcoming "Live in Concert" DVD. During the event, he announced that he would be releasing a new album to be called <i><a href="/wiki/The_Ecstatic" title="The Ecstatic">The Ecstatic</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> He performed a number of new tracks; in later shows, he previewed tracks produced by <a href="/wiki/Madlib" title="Madlib">Madlib</a> and was rumored to be going to <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> for new material. Producer and fellow <a href="/wiki/Def_Poetry_Jam" title="Def Poetry Jam">Def Poet</a> Al Be Back revealed he would be producing on the album as well.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The album was released on June 9, 2009; but only Madlib's production had made the cut, along with tracks by Preservation, <a href="/wiki/The_Neptunes" title="The Neptunes">The Neptunes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mr._Flash" title="Mr. Flash">Mr. Flash</a>, Madlib's brother Oh No, <a href="/wiki/J._Dilla" class="mw-redirect" title="J. Dilla">J. Dilla</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Georgia_Anne_Muldrow" title="Georgia Anne Muldrow">Georgia Anne Muldrow</a>.
</p><p>Bey appears alongside Kanye West on the track "<a href="/wiki/Two_Words" title="Two Words">Two Words</a>" from <i><a href="/wiki/The_College_Dropout" title="The College Dropout">The College Dropout</a></i> album, the track "Drunk and Hot Girls" and the bonus track "Good Night" off West's third major album, <i><a href="/wiki/Graduation_(album)" title="Graduation (album)">Graduation</a></i>. In 2002, he released the 12" single <i>Fine</i>, which was featured in the <i><a href="/wiki/Brown_Sugar_(2002_film)" title="Brown Sugar (2002 film)">Brown Sugar</a></i> Motion Picture Soundtrack.<sup id="cite_ref-Single_Release_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Single_Release-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bey also appears on the debut album from fellow New Yorkers Apollo Heights on a track titled, <i>Concern</i>. In October, he signed a deal with <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Records" title="Downtown Records">Downtown Records</a> and appeared on a remix to the song <i>D.A.N.C.E</i>. by Justice.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> He appeared on <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Marley_(musician)" title="Stephen Marley (musician)">Stephen Marley</a>'s debut album <i><a href="/wiki/Mind_Control_(Stephen_Marley_album)" title="Mind Control (Stephen Marley album)">Mind Control</a></i> on the song "Hey Baby". In 2009, he worked with Somali-Canadian rapper <a href="/wiki/K%27naan" title="K&#39;naan">K'naan</a> to produce the track "America" for K'naan's album <i><a href="/wiki/Troubadour_(K%27naan_album)" title="Troubadour (K&#39;naan album)">Troubadour</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2008, he appeared on the title track for a new album by <a href="/wiki/The_Roots" title="The Roots">The Roots</a> titled <i><a href="/wiki/Rising_Down" title="Rising Down">Rising Down</a></i>. The new single, <i>Life In Marvelous Times</i>, was made officially available through <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> on November 4, 2008, and was also available for <a href="/wiki/Streaming_audio" class="mw-redirect" title="Streaming audio">stream</a> on the Roots' website Okayplayer.
</p><p>In April 2009, Bey traveled to South Africa for the first time, and performed with The <a href="/wiki/Robert_Glasper" title="Robert Glasper">Robert Glasper</a> Experiment at the renowned Cape Town International Jazz Festival. He treated the South African audience with an encore, introduced by his own rendition of <a href="/wiki/John_Coltrane" title="John Coltrane">John Coltrane</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/A_Love_Supreme" title="A Love Supreme">A Love Supreme</a></i>, followed by a sneak preview of the track "M.D. (Doctor)".<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bey has designed two pairs of limited edition <a href="/wiki/Converse_(shoe_company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Converse (shoe company)">Converse</a> shoes. The shoes were released through <a href="/wiki/Foot_Locker" title="Foot Locker">Foot Locker</a> stores on August 1, 2009, in limited amounts.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In late 2009, he created his own clothing line with the "UNDRCRWN" brand called the "Mos Def Cut &amp; Sew Collection". The items were released in select U.S. stores and almost exclusively on the UNDRCRWN website.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> That year, he was among the MCs aligned with American entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Damon_Dash" title="Damon Dash">Damon Dash</a>'s <a href="/wiki/DD172" title="DD172">DD172</a> and collaborating with American blues rock band <a href="/wiki/The_Black_Keys" title="The Black Keys">the Black Keys</a> on the <i><a href="/wiki/Blakroc" title="Blakroc">Blakroc</a></i> album, a project headed by the Black Keys and Damon Dash.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Bey appeared with Harlem-bred rapper <a href="/wiki/Jim_Jones_(rapper)" title="Jim Jones (rapper)">Jim Jones</a> and the Black Keys on <a href="/wiki/Late_Show_with_David_Letterman" title="Late Show with David Letterman">the Late Show with David Letterman</a> to perform the <i>Blakroc</i> track "Ain't Nothing Like You (Hoochie Coo)".
</p><p>In March 2010, Bey's song "Quiet Dog Bite Hard" was featured in Palm's "Life moves fast. Don't miss a thing." campaign.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Bey features on the first single, "<a href="/wiki/Stylo_(song)" title="Stylo (song)">Stylo</a>", from the third <a href="/wiki/Gorillaz" title="Gorillaz">Gorillaz</a> album, <i><a href="/wiki/Plastic_Beach" title="Plastic Beach">Plastic Beach</a></i>, alongside soul legend <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Womack" title="Bobby Womack">Bobby Womack</a>. He also appears on the track titled "Sweepstakes".
</p><p>In September 2010, after appearing on Kanye West's <a href="/wiki/G.O.O.D._Fridays" class="mw-redirect" title="G.O.O.D. Fridays">G.O.O.D. Friday</a> track "Lord Lord Lord", Bey confirmed he had signed with <a href="/wiki/GOOD_Music" title="GOOD Music">GOOD Music</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Bey has been an active contributor to the recovery of the oil spill in the Gulf, performing concerts and raising money towards repairing its damages. In June 2010, he recorded a cover of the classic New Orleans song originally by <a href="/wiki/Smokey_Johnson" title="Smokey Johnson">Smokey Johnson</a>, "<a href="/wiki/It_Ain%27t_My_Fault_(Silkk_the_Shocker_song)" title="It Ain&#39;t My Fault (Silkk the Shocker song)">It Ain't My Fault</a>" with the <a href="/wiki/Preservation_Hall_Jazz_Band" title="Preservation Hall Jazz Band">Preservation Hall Jazz Band</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lenny_Kravitz" title="Lenny Kravitz">Lenny Kravitz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trombone_Shorty" title="Trombone Shorty">Trombone Shorty</a>.
</p><p>In September 2011, the rapper announced that he legally changed his name to Yasiin Bey and would go by that name, retiring his Mos Def moniker.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Bey told a reporter "I began to fear that Mos Def was being treated as a product, not a person, so I’ve been going by Yasiin since ’99. At first it was just for friends and family, but now I'm declaring it openly."<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Bey also stated "Mos Def is a name that I built and cultivated over the years, it's a name that the streets taught me, a figure of speech that was given to me by the culture and by my environment, and I feel I've done quite a bit with that name. ...it's time to expand and move on."<sup id="cite_ref-GSM_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GSM-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Yasiin is a name in the Qur'an's 36th surah and was important to the rapper who converted to Islam in his teens. Bey said the name change would eliminate "having any moniker or separation between the self that I see and know myself as."<sup id="cite_ref-GSM_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GSM-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Shortly after the name change announcement, Bey recorded as the narrator of the children's hip hop musical, Pacha's Pajamas: A Story Written By Nature.
</p>
<h3><span id="2012.E2.80.93present:_Later_career_and_retirement"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012–present:_Later_career_and_retirement">2012–present: Later career and retirement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mos_Def&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2012–present: Later career and retirement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In January 2012, it was reported that Bey and <a href="/wiki/Talib_Kweli" title="Talib Kweli">Talib Kweli</a> had begun "to resurrect" <a href="/wiki/Black_Star_(rap_duo)" title="Black Star (rap duo)">Black Star</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, Bey was featured on <a href="/wiki/A$AP_Rocky" class="mw-redirect" title="A$AP Rocky">A$AP Rocky</a>'s second studio album <i><a href="/wiki/At._Long._Last._ASAP" title="At. Long. Last. ASAP">At. Long. Last. ASAP</a></i>, on the track "Back Home", alongside Acyde and the deceased A$AP Yams.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Bey again revived his Mos Def moniker for two new songs in August 2015, titled "Basquiat Ghostwriter" and "Sensei on the Block", respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 19, 2016, Bey announced his retirement from both the music and film industries on Kanye West's website: "I'm retiring from the music recording industry as it is currently assembled today, and also <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_(film_industry)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hollywood (film industry)">Hollywood</a>, effective immediately. I'm releasing my final album this year, and that's that."<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> After announcing his retirement, he expressed gratitude to everyone who has supported him over the years and revealed his intention to enter the <a href="/wiki/Fashion_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Fashion industry">fashion industry</a> and complete a handful of films.<sup id="cite_ref-hnhh_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hnhh-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Bey also confirmed he still planned to release a collaborative project with <a href="/wiki/Ferrari_Sheppard" title="Ferrari Sheppard">Ferrari Sheppard</a> called <a href="/wiki/Dec_99th" title="Dec 99th">Dec 99th</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hnhh_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hnhh-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2016, a planned concert in London was cancelled due to travel restrictions imposed on the artist;<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> other European dates suffered the same fate.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> On October 14, Bey posted a video to Facebook where he announced that he was still planning to retire: "I'm retiring for real this year, this week. With the 17th anniversary of <i>Black on Both Sides</i> being released, I am grateful to have had the career that I have been able to enjoy."<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> He also announced one last concert which he said he would be live streaming from Cape Town, South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> In November 2016, he was granted the ability to leave but not reenter South Africa and was put on "South Africa's 'undesirable persons' list". He said he would perform one show in Harlem and three in Washington D.C. after leaving South Africa. He announced that Dec 99th, his final album, would be released on December 9. He released three singles from it, "Local Time", "N.A.W." and "Seaside Panic Room".<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> On December 5, 2016, he announced the title of two albums, <i>Negus in Natural Person</i> and <i>As Promised</i>, the latter of which is a collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Southern_hip_hop" title="Southern hip hop">Southern hip hop</a> producer <a href="/wiki/Mannie_Fresh" title="Mannie Fresh">Mannie Fresh</a>, initially titled <i>OMFGOD</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> His claims of retirement were seen as questionable as he played shows on September 13, 2017, at the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Oakland_Theatre" title="Fox Oakland Theatre">Fox Theater</a> in Oakland as part of Black Star and performed on Gorillaz' <a href="/wiki/Humanz_Tour" title="Humanz Tour">Humanz World Tour</a>, performing "Stylo" with Peven Everett, who filled in for Bobby Womack, who died in 2014. He also has yet to release or announce a release date for the last two albums of his career.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In February 2018, Bey announced, on stage, a new Black Star studio album, produced by <a href="/wiki/Madlib" title="Madlib">Madlib</a>, would be released in 2018. However, no specific release date was made available. Later on that year, Bey appeared on the <a href="/wiki/Kids_See_Ghosts_(song)" title="Kids See Ghosts (song)">titular track</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Kids_See_Ghosts_(album)" title="Kids See Ghosts (album)">Kids See Ghosts</a></i>, the collaborative effort of Kanye West and <a href="/wiki/Kid_Cudi" title="Kid Cudi">Kid Cudi</a>. In March 2019, he debuted his album, <i><a href="/wiki/Negus_(album)" class="mw-redirect" title="Negus (album)">ንጉሥ (pronounced Negus)</a></i> at a listening session as part of Art Basel Hong Kong. In a press release, he said that the album "will continue to unfold as a series of varied installations around the world". He has no plans of releasing the album digitally or physically.<sup id="cite_ref-negus_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-negus-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 28, 2019, Bey appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/Bandana_(album)" title="Bandana (album)">Bandana</a></i>, an album by <a href="/wiki/Freddie_Gibbs" title="Freddie Gibbs">Freddie Gibbs</a> and Madlib, alongside <a href="/wiki/Black_Thought" title="Black Thought">Black Thought</a>, on a track named "Education". In November 2019, he stated that unreleased music, such as his collaborative album with Mannie Fresh, was still "on deck" for release.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> In 2021, he launched "The Midnight Miracle" podcast on <a href="/wiki/Luminary_(podcast_network)" title="Luminary (podcast network)">Luminary</a>, along with <a href="/wiki/Dave_Chappelle" title="Dave Chappelle">Dave Chappelle</a> and Talib Kweli.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> In April 2022, a release date for the long-awaited Black Star project was officially announced. The album titled <i><a href="/wiki/No_Fear_of_Time" title="No Fear of Time">No Fear of Time</a></i> was released via Luminary on May 3, 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Acting_career">Acting career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mos_Def&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Acting career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Beginnings_as_child_actor">Beginnings as child actor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mos_Def&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Beginnings as child actor">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Prior to his career in music, Bey entered public life as a child actor, having played roles in <a href="/wiki/Television_movies" class="mw-redirect" title="Television movies">television movies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sitcoms" class="mw-redirect" title="Sitcoms">sitcoms</a> and <a href="/wiki/Theater" class="mw-redirect" title="Theater">theater</a>, some of which were under the name Dante Beze.<sup id="cite_ref-HHS_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HHS-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-IMDB_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IMDB-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> At the age of 14, he appeared in the TV movie <i><a href="/wiki/God_Bless_the_Child_(film)" title="God Bless the Child (film)">God Bless the Child</a></i>, starring <a href="/wiki/Mare_Winningham" title="Mare Winningham">Mare Winningham</a>, which aired on ABC in 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> He played the oldest child in the 1990 family sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/You_Take_the_Kids" title="You Take the Kids">You Take the Kids</a></i>, shortly before it was cancelled. In 1995, he played the character Dante, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Cosby" title="Bill Cosby">Bill Cosby</a>'s sidekick on the short-lived detective show <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cosby_Mysteries" title="The Cosby Mysteries">The Cosby Mysteries</a></i>. In 1996, he starred in a <a href="/wiki/Visa_Inc." title="Visa Inc.">Visa</a> check card commercial featuring <a href="/wiki/Deion_Sanders" title="Deion Sanders">Deion Sanders</a>. He also had a small role alongside <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a> in his short film and music video <i><a href="/wiki/Ghosts_(1997_film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ghosts (1997 film)">Ghosts</a></i> (1997).
</p>
<h3><span id="Feature_films.2C_theater_and_television"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Feature_films,_theater_and_television">Feature films, theater and television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mos_Def&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Feature films, theater and television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After brief appearances in <i><a href="/wiki/Bamboozled" title="Bamboozled">Bamboozled</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Monster%27s_Ball" title="Monster&#39;s Ball">Monster's Ball</a></i>, Bey played a rapper who is reluctant to sign with a major label in <i><a href="/wiki/Brown_Sugar_(2002_film)" title="Brown Sugar (2002 film)">Brown Sugar</a></i>. He was nominated for an <a href="/wiki/Image_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Image Award">Image Award</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Teen_Choice_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Teen Choice Award">Teen Choice Award</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2001, he took a supporting role to <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9_Knowles" class="mw-redirect" title="Beyoncé Knowles">Beyoncé Knowles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mehki_Phifer" class="mw-redirect" title="Mehki Phifer">Mehki Phifer</a> in the <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a> movie <i><a href="/wiki/Carmen:_A_Hip_Hopera" title="Carmen: A Hip Hopera">Carmen: A Hip Hopera</a></i> as Lt. Miller, a crooked cop.
</p><p>In 2002, he played the role of Booth in <a href="/wiki/Suzan-Lori_Parks" title="Suzan-Lori Parks">Suzan-Lori Parks</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/Topdog/Underdog" title="Topdog/Underdog">Topdog/Underdog</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Tony Award">Tony</a>-nominated and <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer</a>-winning <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">Broadway</a> play. He and co-star Jeffrey Wright won a Special Award from the Outer Critics Circle Award for their joint performance.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> He played Left Ear in the 2003 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Italian_Job_(2003_film)" title="The Italian Job (2003 film)">The Italian Job</a></i>. That same year, he appeared in the <a href="/wiki/Alicia_Keys" title="Alicia Keys">Alicia Keys</a> music video <a href="/wiki/You_Don%27t_Know_My_Name#Music_video" title="You Don&#39;t Know My Name">You Don't Know My Name</a>.
</p><p>In television, Bey has appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/NYPD_Blue" title="NYPD Blue">NYPD Blue</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Comedy_Central" title="Comedy Central">Comedy Central</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Chappelle%27s_Show" title="Chappelle&#39;s Show">Chappelle's Show</a></i>, and hosted the award-winning <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a> <a href="/wiki/Spoken_word" title="Spoken word">spoken word</a> show <i><a href="/wiki/Def_Poetry" class="mw-redirect" title="Def Poetry">Def Poetry</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> He also appeared on the sitcom <i><a href="/wiki/My_Wife_and_Kids" title="My Wife and Kids">My Wife and Kids</a></i> as the disabled friend of Michael Kyle (<a href="/wiki/Damon_Wayans" title="Damon Wayans">Damon Wayans</a>).
</p><p>Bey won "Best Actor, Independent Movie" at the 2005 <a href="/wiki/Black_Reel_Awards" title="Black Reel Awards">Black Reel Awards</a> for his portrayal of Detective Sgt. Lucas in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Woodsman_(2004_film)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Woodsman (2004 film)">The Woodsman</a></i>. For his portrayal of <a href="/wiki/Vivien_Thomas" title="Vivien Thomas">Vivien Thomas</a> in <a href="/wiki/HBO" title="HBO">HBO</a>'s film <i><a href="/wiki/Something_the_Lord_Made" title="Something the Lord Made">Something the Lord Made</a></i>, he was nominated for an <a href="/wiki/Emmy" class="mw-redirect" title="Emmy">Emmy</a><sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Globe">Golden Globe</a>, and won the <a href="/wiki/Image_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Image Award">Image Award</a>. He also played a bandleader in HBO's <i><a href="/wiki/Lackawanna_Blues_(film)" title="Lackawanna Blues (film)">Lackawanna Blues</a></i>. He then landed the role of <a href="/wiki/Ford_Prefect_(character)" title="Ford Prefect (character)">Ford Prefect</a> in the 2005 movie adaptation of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hitchhiker%27s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy_(film)" title="The Hitchhiker&#39;s Guide to the Galaxy (film)">The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy</a></i>.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Def_Willis.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Def_Willis.jpg/220px-Def_Willis.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Def_Willis.jpg/330px-Def_Willis.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Def_Willis.jpg/440px-Def_Willis.jpg 2x" data-file-width="492" data-file-height="340" /></a><figcaption>Yasiin Bey and <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Willis" title="Bruce Willis">Bruce Willis</a> on the set of <i><a href="/wiki/16_Blocks" title="16 Blocks">16 Blocks</a></i>, filmed on location in <a href="/wiki/Chinatown,_Manhattan" title="Chinatown, Manhattan">Chinatown, Manhattan</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>In 2006, Bey appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/Dave_Chappelle%27s_Block_Party" title="Dave Chappelle&#39;s Block Party">Dave Chappelle's Block Party</a></i> alongside <a href="/wiki/Black_Star_(rap_duo)" title="Black Star (rap duo)">Black Star</a> partner <a href="/wiki/Talib_Kweli" title="Talib Kweli">Talib Kweli</a>, while also contributing to the film's soundtrack. He was also featured as the <a href="/wiki/Banjo" title="Banjo">banjo</a> player in the Pixie Sketch" from <i>Chappelle's Show: The Lost Episodes</i>, though his appearance was edited out of the DVD. He starred in the action film <i><a href="/wiki/16_Blocks" title="16 Blocks">16 Blocks</a></i> alongside <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Willis" title="Bruce Willis">Bruce Willis</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Morse_(actor)" class="mw-redirect" title="David Morse (actor)">David Morse</a>. He also landed a recurring guest role on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Boondocks_(TV_series)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Boondocks (TV series)">Boondocks</a></i>, starring as Gangstalicious. He is set to be in <i>Toussaint</i>, a film about <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haitian</a> revolutionary <a href="/wiki/Toussaint_Louverture" title="Toussaint Louverture">Toussaint Louverture</a>, opposite <a href="/wiki/Don_Cheadle" title="Don Cheadle">Don Cheadle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wesley_Snipes" title="Wesley Snipes">Wesley Snipes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> He made a cameo appearance as himself in the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Talladega_Nights:_The_Ballad_of_Ricky_Bobby" title="Talladega Nights: The Ballad of Ricky Bobby">Talladega Nights: The Ballad of Ricky Bobby</a></i>.
</p><p>In 2007, Bey narrated the PBS-broadcast documentary <i><a href="/wiki/Prince_Among_Slaves_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince Among Slaves (film)">Prince Among Slaves</a></i>.
</p><p>In 2008, Bey starred in the <a href="/wiki/Michel_Gondry" title="Michel Gondry">Michel Gondry</a> movie <i><a href="/wiki/Be_Kind_Rewind" title="Be Kind Rewind">Be Kind Rewind</a></i>, playing a video rental store employee whose best friend is played by co-star <a href="/wiki/Jack_Black" title="Jack Black">Jack Black</a>. He also portrayed <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Berry" title="Chuck Berry">Chuck Berry</a> in the film <i><a href="/wiki/Cadillac_Records" title="Cadillac Records">Cadillac Records</a></i>, for which he was nominated for a <a href="/wiki/Black_Reel_Awards" title="Black Reel Awards">Black Reel Award</a> and an <a href="/wiki/Image_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Image Awards">Image Award</a>.
</p><p>In 2009, he appeared in the <i><a href="/wiki/House_(TV_series)" title="House (TV series)">House</a></i> episode titled "<a href="/wiki/House_(season_5)#ep105" title="House (season 5)">Locked In</a>" as a patient suffering from <a href="/wiki/Locked-in_syndrome" title="Locked-in syndrome">locked-in syndrome</a>. His performance was well received, with <a href="/wiki/E!" title="E!">E!</a> saying that Mos Def "delivers an <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Emmy Award">Emmy</a>-worthy performance".<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> He was also in the 2009 film <i><a href="/wiki/Next_Day_Air" title="Next Day Air">Next Day Air</a></i>.
</p><p>In 2010, he appeared on the children's show <i><a href="/wiki/Yo_Gabba_Gabba!" title="Yo Gabba Gabba!">Yo Gabba Gabba!</a></i> as Super Mr. Superhero. He also appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/A_Free_Man_of_Color" title="A Free Man of Color">A Free Man of Color</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/John_Guare" title="John Guare">John Guare</a>'s play at the <a href="/wiki/Vivian_Beaumont_Theatre" class="mw-redirect" title="Vivian Beaumont Theatre">Vivian Beaumont Theatre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2011, he began a multi-episode appearance on the sixth season of <a href="/wiki/Showtime_(TV_network)" title="Showtime (TV network)">Showtime</a> television series <i><a href="/wiki/Dexter_(TV_series)" title="Dexter (TV series)">Dexter</a></i>. He played Brother Sam, an ex-convict who has supposedly found religion despite finding himself in violent situations.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2016, Bey announced his retirement from the music and the film industries on Kanye West's website. In March 2016, it was announced that he had been attached to star in "his last live-action film", <i>The Disconnected</i>, a <a href="/wiki/Science_fiction" title="Science fiction">science fiction</a> thriller dealing with policing, identity, and the intersection of technology and humanity.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_and_political_views">Social and political views</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mos_Def&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Social and political views">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2000, paired with <a href="/wiki/Talib_Kweli" title="Talib Kweli">Talib Kweli</a>, Bey organized the <a href="/wiki/Hip_Hop_for_Respect" title="Hip Hop for Respect">Hip Hop for Respect</a> project to speak out against police brutality. It was created in response to the 1999 police <a href="/wiki/Shooting_of_Amadou_Diallo" class="mw-redirect" title="Shooting of Amadou Diallo">shooting of Amadou Diallo</a>, and sought to accumulate 41 artists to the roster, one to match each of the 41 gunshots fired on Diallo.
</p><p>Bey is well known for his <a href="/wiki/Modern_liberalism_in_the_United_States" title="Modern liberalism in the United States">leftist</a> activism.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> In 2000, he performed a benefit concert for death row inmate <a href="/wiki/Mumia_Abu-Jamal" title="Mumia Abu-Jamal">Mumia Abu-Jamal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> In May 2005, Bey, Talib Kweli, R&amp;B singer Martin Luther and City Councilman <a href="/wiki/Charles_Barron" title="Charles Barron">Charles Barron</a> approached New York City Hall, demanding the withdrawal of the $1 million bounty for <a href="/wiki/Assata_Shakur" title="Assata Shakur">Assata Shakur</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2005, Bey released the single "Katrina Clap", renamed "Dollar Day" for <i>True Magic</i> (utilizing the instrumental for <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a> rappers UTP's "<a href="/wiki/Nolia_Clap" title="Nolia Clap">Nolia Clap</a>"). The song is a <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_the_government_response_to_Hurricane_Katrina" title="Criticism of the government response to Hurricane Katrina">criticism</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_George_W._Bush" title="Presidency of George W. Bush">Bush administration</a>'s response to <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a>. On the night of the <a href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards" title="MTV Video Music Awards">MTV Video Music Awards</a>, Bey pulled up in front of <a href="/wiki/Radio_City_Music_Hall" title="Radio City Music Hall">Radio City Music Hall</a> on a flatbed truck and began performing the "Katrina Clap" single in front of a crowd that quickly gathered around him. He was subsequently arrested for not having a public performance permit in his possession.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In October 2006, Bey appeared on <i>4Real</i>, a documentary television series.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Appearing in the episode "City of God", he and the 4Real crew traveled to <a href="/wiki/Cidade_de_Deus_(Rio_de_Janeiro)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cidade de Deus (Rio de Janeiro)">City of God</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Favela" title="Favela">favela</a> in Rio de Janeiro, Brazil, to meet Brazilian MC <a href="/wiki/MV_Bill" title="MV Bill">MV Bill</a> and learn about the crime and social problems of the community.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On September 7, 2007, Bey appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/Real_Time_with_Bill_Maher" title="Real Time with Bill Maher">Real Time with Bill Maher</a></i> where he spoke about <a href="/wiki/Racism_in_the_United_States" title="Racism in the United States">racism</a> against <a href="/wiki/African_Americans" title="African Americans">African Americans</a>, citing the <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_the_government_response_to_Hurricane_Katrina" title="Criticism of the government response to Hurricane Katrina">government response to Hurricane Katrina</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Jena_Six" title="Jena Six">Jena Six</a> case, and the murder conviction of <a href="/wiki/Mumia_Abu-Jamal" title="Mumia Abu-Jamal">Mumia Abu-Jamal</a>. He appeared on <i>Real Time</i> again on March 27, 2009, and spoke about the risk of <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_weapon" title="Nuclear weapon">nuclear weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2011, Bey joined the cast of the environmental children's hip hop musical <i>Pacha's Pajamas: A Story Written By Nature</i> as narrator. In July 2013, he appeared in a short film released by the human rights organization <a href="/wiki/Reprieve_(organisation)" title="Reprieve (organisation)">Reprieve</a>, depicting the <a href="/wiki/Guantanamo_force_feeding" title="Guantanamo force feeding">forced-feeding</a> methods used at the <a href="/wiki/Guantanamo_Bay_detention_camp" title="Guantanamo Bay detention camp">Guantanamo Bay</a> detention camps. This transpired after a document containing the military instructions for the procedure was leaked.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2018, Bey and advertising executive Free Richardson opened an art exhibition to the public in an art gallery in the South Bronx, called the Compound, centered around hip-hop and fine art. The goal of this gallery was to help bridge the gap between the two fields, by showcasing artists from marginalized backgrounds who normally would not be represented in art galleries. Art forms with negative connotations, such as graffiti, as presented in a more optimal context. "The purpose of the gallery is to say all art is equal," Mr. Richardson said. "But we are in the borough that created hip-hop, which is the biggest art form in the world, so it's always an extending arm. It's always present."<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mos_Def&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/About.com" class="mw-redirect" title="About.com">About.com</a> ranked him #14 on its list of the Top 50 MCs of Our Time,<sup id="cite_ref-:1_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Source_(magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Source (magazine)">The Source</a></i> ranked him #23 on their list of the Top 50 Lyricists of All Time.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/AllMusic" title="AllMusic">AllMusic</a> called him one of the most promising rappers to emerge in the late 1990s,<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> and one of hip-hop's brightest hopes entering the 21st century.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic1_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic1-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> He has influenced numerous hip hop artists throughout his career, including <a href="/wiki/Lupe_Fiasco" title="Lupe Fiasco">Lupe Fiasco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jay_Electronica" title="Jay Electronica">Jay Electronica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kid_Cudi" title="Kid Cudi">Kid Cudi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Saigon_(rapper)" title="Saigon (rapper)">Saigon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a> once mentioned him as a very early inspiration as a young rapper, though Lamar denied being a part of the conscious rap movement.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> He has also directly influenced artists outside of hip-hop, including English singer-songwriters <a href="/wiki/Adele" title="Adele">Adele</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amy_Winehouse" title="Amy Winehouse">Amy Winehouse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mos_Def&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Bey married Maria Yepes in 1996. He filed for divorce from Yepes in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> She took him to court over failure in child-support obligations, paying $2,000 short of the monthly $10,000 he is ordered to pay for their two daughters.<sup id="cite_ref-NYP_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYP-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> He has four other children.<sup id="cite_ref-TheStar_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TheStar-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>His mother Sheron "Umi" Smith has actively managed portions of her son's career.<sup id="cite_ref-YasiinDef_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YasiinDef-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> She is a motivational speaker, and authored the book <i>Shine Your Light: A Life Skills Workbook</i>, where she details her experience as a single mother raising him.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2016, Bey was ordered to leave South Africa and not return for five years, having stayed in the country illegally on an expired tourist visa granted in May 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> That month, he was charged with using an unrecognized <a href="/wiki/World_Passport" title="World Passport">World Passport</a> and having lived illegally in South Africa since 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> He had reportedly recruited <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> to help defend him, and posted a message on West's website announcing his retirement from show business.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> There was an ongoing court case in relation to immigration offenses involving the artist and his family.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> He was allowed to leave South Africa on November 22, 2016, but he was barred from coming back.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mos_Def&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Discography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Mos_Def_discography" title="Mos Def discography">Mos Def discography</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_songs_recorded_by_Mos_Def" title="List of songs recorded by Mos Def">List of songs recorded by Mos Def</a></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mos_Def&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-upper-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-109"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-109">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>Negus</i> is Yasiin Bey’s fifth studio album, entirely produced by Lord Tusk, Steven Julien, and ACyde and was recorded in London in 2015. <i>Negus</i> was exclusively premiered during Art Basel in Hong Kong on March 29, 2019. According to a press release, the album will never receive a physical or digital release but will be displayed at sound installations around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
